              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16058487886276559896">I almost want to give it that third star, but the melodrama didn't really start until three quarters of the way through. Before the fun stuff was a bunch of occasional musing on Martha's part about Alice, and no real searching. And I have no idea why Connan was such a catch. He was a jerk, Martha disliked him, Martha got a crush, Connan liked her interest, Martha loves children, Martha loves Connan, Connan loves Martha. So unlike the infamous gold-standard Mr. Darcy, Connan's full character arc </span>
  <span id="freeText16058487886276559896" style="display:none">I almost want to give it that third star, but the melodrama didn't really start until three quarters of the way through. Before the fun stuff was a bunch of occasional musing on Martha's part about Alice, and no real searching. And I have no idea why Connan was such a catch. He was a jerk, Martha disliked him, Martha got a crush, Connan liked her interest, Martha loves children, Martha loves Connan, Connan loves Martha. So unlike the infamous gold-standard Mr. Darcy, Connan's full character arc goes from arrogant sot to besotted without, you know, ever actually overcoming his obnoxiousness. <br /><br />And I read a <i>lot</i> of Holt in middle school—I seem to recall a full shelf of them for some reason—and now I'm wondering if I always found the protagonists so vaguely unlikable. Martha <i>does</i> so little, up unto fainting until rescue. She tries for spunky without ever being quite clever enough to manage.<br /><br />But Alvean and Gilly were good child characters, which is something I'm sensitive too, and I did like their growing relationship with Martha, though, given this novel is from Martha's perspective, I really could barely tell it was happening on her part. And of course, the melodrama was fun, when it arrived.</span>

<div id="review_40469956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40469956" />
    <a title="Meagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/270740-meagan"><img alt="Meagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567024760p2/270740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40469956?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meagan" href="/user/show/270740-meagan">Meagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312384159" href="/book/show/6004636-mistress-of-mellyn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/270740-meagan?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/270740-meagan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/270740-meagan?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40469956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4509898414237578232"><i>Mistress of Mellyn</i> is a great example of an old-fashioned gothic romance. It begins with the necessary heroine, an impoverished gentlewoman with no prospects for marriage (of course), who is pursuing a living as a governess in an isolated and somewhat spooky manor. The master of the house is a widower, handsome and forbidding, whose wife died in fantastic circumstances and whose body was never positively identified. All this is wrapped up in rumors and mysterious happenings while our heroine, ag</span>
  <span id="freeText4509898414237578232" style="display:none"><i>Mistress of Mellyn</i> is a great example of an old-fashioned gothic romance. It begins with the necessary heroine, an impoverished gentlewoman with no prospects for marriage (of course), who is pursuing a living as a governess in an isolated and somewhat spooky manor. The master of the house is a widower, handsome and forbidding, whose wife died in fantastic circumstances and whose body was never positively identified. All this is wrapped up in rumors and mysterious happenings while our heroine, against all her better judgment, begins to have feelings for the man she suspects may have had a hand in his wife's death. It's sentimental, full of cliches, over the top, and immensely entertaining reading. If you like your romances of the soap-opera variety, with the threat of doom and gloom, Victoria Holt in general and <i>Mistress of Mellyn</i> in particular will serve you well!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4509898414237578232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60277926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6075659894383776516"><i> We are born, we suffer, we love, we die, but the waves continue to beat upon the rocks; the seed time and the harvest come and go, but the earth remains. </i></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TxPO7oeXp5n3EnRT0ZyzEvN2pSiCQ1Xq0Vn7iZzczHAaZZyIlwKK4wx/r1PnXeG9gK6dLHInCJG3i9vCaJX3jw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eM1sJZIYM9IwBr9wpp7KukLNJ2RK/QhOCpcxaf2kPdctuz5Dgo0eqMtrZHCQX5gVMRUfYLqZVTVsRREiCe0GKA==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer13539534914895216893"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br/><br/>Eleanor Alice Burford, Mrs. George Percival Hibbert was a British author of about 200 historical novels, most of them under the pen name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6590.Jean_Plaidy' title='Jean Plaidy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jean Plaidy</a> which had sold 14 million copies by the time of her death. She chose to use various names because of the differences in subjec</span>
  <span id="freeText13539534914895216893" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />Eleanor Alice Burford, Mrs. George Percival Hibbert was a British author of about 200 historical novels, most of them under the pen name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6590.Jean_Plaidy" title="Jean Plaidy" rel="nofollow noopener">Jean Plaidy</a> which had sold 14 million copies by the time of her death. She chose to use various names because of the differences in subject matter between her books; the best-known, apart from Plaidy, are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25092.Victoria_Holt" title="Victoria Holt" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holt</a> (56 million) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/32.Philippa_Carr" title="Philippa Carr" rel="nofollow noopener">Philippa Carr</a> (3 million). Lesser known were the novels Hibbert published under her maiden name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1411371.Eleanor_Burford" title="Eleanor Burford" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor Burford</a>, or the pseudonyms of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2931390.Elbur_Ford" title="Elbur Ford" rel="nofollow noopener">Elbur Ford</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2931417.Kathleen_Kellow" title="Kathleen Kellow" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen Kellow</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1002136.Ellalice_Tate" title="Ellalice Tate" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellalice Tate</a>. Many of her readers under one penname never suspected her other identities.<br />-Wikipedia<br /></span>
